Iteration 6 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based **strictly** on the provided Evidence keys. You must act as a strict logic gate: if the specific fact, location, or relationship asserted in the claim is not explicitly represented by a key in the Evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects. Each object has a `key` (string) and a `value` (integer).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **Value 0**: In this specific dataset, a `value` of `0` indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **IS PRESENT** and relevant to the context. It does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat any key with a value (0 or otherwise) as a confirmed fact.
- **Value > 0**: Also indicates presence.
- **Absence**: If a specific entity or fact is not listed as a `key` at all, it is considered absent.

### 2. The "Strict Matching" Verification Strategy
The core logic of this task is **not** about checking if names co-occur, but about checking if the **specific attributes** or **relationships** asserted in the claim are explicitly present as keys.

- **Rule A: Specific Entity Matching**
  - If a claim asserts a specific entity (e.g., "born in [Location X]", "played character [Name Y]"), the Evidence **must** contain a key that matches that specific entity exactly.
  - **Mismatch Logic**: If the claim says "New York County" but the evidence only has "Hoosick, New York", the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**. Do not infer that "Hoosick" is inside "New York County" unless the evidence explicitly contains the key "New York County".
  - **Name Confusion**: If a claim asserts "Actress X played Character Y" (where Y is a character name), the evidence must contain the key "Character Y". If the evidence only contains "Actress X" and the Show Name, but not "Character Y", the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Rule B: Relationship and Attribute Verification**
  - **Mere Co-occurrence is Insufficient**: The presence of two names (e.g., "Person A" and "Person B") in the evidence keys does **NOT** support a claim that asserts a specific relationship between them (e.g., "A broke B's record" or "A wrote about B") unless the Evidence also contains a key representing that specific relationship or the specific fact.
  - **Exception (Record Breaking)**: In the specific context of "Record Breaking" claims (e.g., "X broke Y's record"), the co-occurrence of the Record Holder and the Record Breaker keys is sufficient to support the claim.
  - **General Relationships**: For all other relationships (e.g., "X is in Y's repertoire", "X wrote 4 books about Y", "X played character Z"), the Evidence **must** contain a key explicitly describing that relationship or the specific attribute (e.g., a key like "Bellini in Callas repertoire" or "Ardoin books about Callas"). If only the names exist, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Rule C: Numerical/Factual Claims**
  - If a claim asserts a specific number (e.g., "94 episodes"), the Evidence **must** contain a key representing that number or the specific fact (e.g., "94 episodes"). If the evidence only lists the show name, the numerical claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Decision Rule
- **SUPPORTED**: ONLY if the Evidence keys contain the **exact specific entities**, **locations**, **numbers**, or **relationship descriptors** required to prove every specific assertion in the claim.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If:
  1. A critical specific entity (location, character name, number) asserted in the claim is missing from the Evidence keys.
  2. The Evidence provides a contradictory entity (e.g., Claim says "Location A", Evidence has "Location B").
  3. The claim asserts a relationship (other than the specific "Record Breaking" exception) that is not explicitly represented by a relationship key in the Evidence.

## Reasoning Steps
1.  **Deconstruct the Claim**: Identify the Subject, the Predicate (the specific action/relationship), and the Object (target, location, number, character name).
2.  **Scan Evidence for Exact Matches**:
    - Look for keys that match the **specific** components identified in Step 1.
    - **Do not** rely on inference. If the claim says "Character Name", look for "Character Name". If the claim says "Location X", look for "Location X".
    - Check if the Evidence contains keys representing the specific relationship asserted.
3.  **Apply Logic**:
    - If all specific components are found as keys: **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any specific component is missing or contradicted: **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**:
    - Provide a brief reasoning summary.
    - **MANDATORY**: End your response with the final verdict on a new line in the format: `Verdict: SUPPORTED` or `Verdict: NOT_SUPPORTED`.

## Example Application

**Example 1: Location Mismatch**
- **Claim**: "Lyman Sherwood was born in New York County."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Lyman Sherwood', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Hoosick, New York', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**: The claim asserts the birth location is "New York County". The evidence contains "Hoosick, New York". These are distinct keys. The specific key "New York County" is missing.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

**Example 2: Missing Relationship Key**
- **Claim**: "Vincenzo Bellini was in Maria Callas's repertoire."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Maria Callas', 'value': 2}`, `{'key': 'Vincenzo Bellini', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**: The claim asserts a specific relationship ("in repertoire"). The evidence only lists the two names separately. There is no key representing the relationship "Bellini in Callas repertoire". Mere co-occurrence is insufficient.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

**Example 3: Record Breaking (Exception)**
- **Claim**: "Mike Hessman broke Buzz Arlett's record."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Buzz Arlett', 'value': 2}`, `{'key': 'Mike Hessman', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**: This is a "Record Breaking" claim. The evidence contains both the Record Holder (Buzz Arlett) and the Record Breaker (Mike Hessman). In this domain, this co-occurrence validates the relationship.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

**Example 4: Missing Character Name**
- **Claim**: "The voice actress of Miss Spider played the character Cynthia Nixon."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Kristin Davis', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Miss Spider', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Sex and the City', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**: The claim asserts the character's name is "Cynthia Nixon". The evidence contains "Kristin Davis" (the actress) and "Miss Spider", but it does **not** contain a key for "Cynthia Nixon" (the character name). The claim conflates the actor's name with a character name, but regardless of real-world facts, the specific key "Cynthia Nixon" is missing from the evidence to support the assertion that she played a character by that name.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

**Example 5: Missing Numerical Fact**
- **Claim**: "94 episodes were in the original run of Sex and the City."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Sex and the City', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**: The claim asserts a specific number ("94 episodes"). The evidence only contains the show name. There is no key representing "94 episodes".
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

Iteration 6 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Based on the analysis of the provided examples, feedback, and the specific conflict in Example 1, here is the refined instruction.

### Analysis of the Task Logic & Domain Specifics

1.  **The Core Conflict (Example 1 vs. Examples 2 & 3)**:
    *   **The "Strict Matching" Trap**: The previous instruction correctly identified that Example 2 (Location mismatch) and Example 3 (Relationship mismatch) required `NOT_SUPPORTED` because the evidence lacked specific keys for "New York County" or "Bellini in Repertoire".
    *   **The Dataset Anomaly (Example 1)**: In Example 1, the claim asserts that two people share **four specific career titles** (actor, writer, producer, director). The evidence *only* lists the two names. The feedback explicitly states this **IS** `SUPPORTED`.
    *   **The Hidden Domain Rule**: This dataset (likely derived from a specific knowledge graph or entity retrieval system like Wikipedia infoboxes or a specific "Person" entity schema) operates on a **"Co-occurrence Implies Shared Attribute"** logic **IF** the claim is a standard "shared profession" assertion.
    *   **Differentiation**:
        *   **Location/Specific Fact Claims**: Require explicit keys for the specific location or fact (e.g., "New York County"). If the key is missing, it's `NOT_SUPPORTED`.
        *   **Shared Profession/Role Claims**: If the claim asserts that two entities share a set of standard professional roles (e.g., "Actor, Writer, Producer, Director"), the **mere presence of both entity names** in the evidence is **sufficient** to support the claim. The system assumes that if two people are retrieved together in this context, they share the queried attributes.
        *   **Complex Relationship Claims**: If the claim asserts a specific, non-standard relationship (e.g., "X wrote 4 books about Y" or "X is in Y's repertoire"), mere co-occurrence is **insufficient**.

2.  **Refined Strategy**:
    *   **Step 1: Categorize the Claim**. Is the claim about a **Specific Location/Date/Fact** OR a **Shared Profession/Role**?
    *   **Step 2: Apply the Correct Rule**.
        *   **Rule A (Specific Location/Fact)**: Strict matching required. If the specific key (e.g., "New York County") is missing, verdict is `NOT_SUPPORTED`.
        *   **Rule B (Shared Profession/Role)**: If the claim asserts that Entity A and Entity B share a list of standard job titles, the presence of **both** Entity A and Entity B in the evidence keys is **sufficient** for `SUPPORTED`. Do not look for keys for "Actor" or "Director".
        *   **Rule C (Specific Narrative/Relationship)**: If the claim asserts a specific event, count, or unique relationship (e.g., "wrote 4 books", "broke record"), check for keys representing that specific relationship. If only names are present, it is `NOT_SUPPORTED` (unless it falls under the specific "Record Breaker" exception seen in Example 1 of the *original* prompt, but Example 3 suggests we must be strict on *counts* and *repertoire*). *Correction*: Looking at Example 1 (Ed Wood/Fernand Rivers) vs Example 3 (Bellini/Callas), the distinction is **General Professional Roles** vs **Specific Narrative Details**.
            *   *Ed Wood/Fernand Rivers*: "Share titles actor, writer..." -> **Supported** (General Roles).
            *   *Bellini/Callas*: "Bellini in repertoire... Ardoin wrote 4 books..." -> **Not Supported** (Specific Narrative/Counts).
            *   *Hessman/Arlett*: "Hessman broke Arlett's record" -> **Supported** (This seems to be a specific "Record" relationship exception, or perhaps "Record Breaker" is treated as a standard role in this dataset).
    *   **Synthesis**: The safest domain rule to encode is: **For claims asserting that two entities share a set of standard professional roles (Actor, Writer, etc.), the co-occurrence of the entity names is sufficient evidence. For all other specific factual assertions (locations, counts, specific relationships, repertoire), strict key matching is required.**

### New Instruction

```markdown
# Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or specific fact) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)
1.  **Interpretation of Evidence Values**: In this specific task, a `value` of `0` indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context. It does **NOT** mean the information is missing.
2.  **Verification Strategy (Context-Dependent Matching)**:
    The verification rule changes based on the **type of assertion** made in the claim. You must first categorize the claim before applying the rule.

    ### Category A: Shared Professional Roles (The "Co-occurrence" Rule)
    - **Definition**: The claim asserts that two or more entities share a set of standard professional titles or roles (e.g., "Actor, Writer, Producer, Director", "Politician, Lawyer", "Doctor, Scientist").
    - **Rule**: If the claim falls into this category, **mere co-occurrence** of the entity names in the Evidence keys is **SUFFICIENT** to support the claim.
    - **Action**: Check if **all** named entities in the claim are present in the Evidence keys.
        - If **all** names are present -> **SUPPORTED**.
        - If **any** name is missing -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    - **Note**: You do **NOT** need to find keys for the specific roles (e.g., "Actor" or "Director") in the evidence. The presence of the people implies the shared roles in this dataset context.

    ### Category B: Specific Facts, Locations, or Narrative Relationships (The "Strict Match" Rule)
    - **Definition**: The claim asserts a specific location (e.g., "born in New York County"), a specific count (e.g., "wrote 4 books"), a specific relationship (e.g., "in the repertoire of"), or a unique event (e.g., "broke a record" - *unless the dataset treats 'record breaker' as a standard role, but generally treat specific counts/locations strictly*).
    - **Rule**: The Evidence **must** contain keys that explicitly match the specific detail asserted.
    - **Action**:
        - **Location**: If the claim says "born in [Location X]", the Evidence **must** contain the key "[Location X]". If the Evidence contains a different location (e.g., "[Location Y]"), it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
        - **Counts/Specific Details**: If the claim says "wrote 4 books", the Evidence **must** contain a key representing that specific fact (e.g., "4 books about X" or a key linking the count). Mere presence of the author's name is **insufficient**.
        - **Relationships**: If the claim says "A is in B's repertoire", the Evidence **must** contain a key representing that specific relationship. Mere presence of A and B is **insufficient**.

    ### Decision Rule Summary
    - **SUPPORTED**:
        1.  (Category A) All named entities are present in the evidence keys.
        2.  (Category B) The specific fact, location, or relationship key asserted in the claim is explicitly present in the evidence keys.
    - **NOT_SUPPORTED**:
        1.  (Category A) One or more named entities are missing.
        2.  (Category B) The specific key for the location/count/relationship is missing, OR the evidence contains a contradictory entity (e.g., Claim: "New York County", Evidence: "Hoosick").

## Reasoning Steps
1.  **Categorize the Claim**:
    - Does the claim assert that entities share **standard professional roles** (Actor, Writer, etc.)? -> **Apply Category A Rule**.
    - Does the claim assert a **specific location, count, unique relationship, or narrative detail**? -> **Apply Category B Rule**.

2.  **Scan Evidence**:
    - **If Category A**: List the names in the claim. Check if every single name exists as a `key` in the Evidence.
    - **If Category B**: Extract the specific predicate (location, count, relationship). Search for a `key` in the Evidence that matches this predicate exactly or represents the specific fact.

3.  **Apply Logic**:
    - **Category A Logic**: If all names are found -> `SUPPORTED`. Else -> `NOT_SUPPORTED`.
    - **Category B Logic**: If the specific detail key is found -> `SUPPORTED`. If the key is missing or contradicts the claim -> `NOT_SUPPORTED`.

4.  **Formulate Conclusion**: State the final verdict clearly as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Example Application

### Example 1 (Category A: Shared Roles)
- **Claim**: "Ed Wood and Fernand

Iteration 6 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Based on the analysis of the provided examples and the specific feedback regarding the "Giuseppe Sermonti" case, there is a critical nuance in the task logic that was misunderstood in the previous iteration.

**Key Insight:**
The task is **not** a strict "exact string match of relationships" task where a key like "Sermonti edited Forum" is required. Instead, the task relies on **implicit relationship validation through co-occurrence** when the evidence keys represent the **primary entities** involved in a well-known factual event.

*   **The Conflict:** The previous instruction correctly identified that "Hoosick" $\neq$ "New York County" (Location Mismatch) and that "Bellini/Callas/Ardoin" co-occurrence was insufficient because the claim asserted specific *quantities* ("4 books") or *specific contexts* ("repertoire") that were not implied by the names alone.
*   **The Correction:** In the "Sermonti" case (and the "Hessman/Arlett" case), the claim asserts a **defining role** (Editor of the Forum / Record Breaker). In this specific dataset context, if the **Subject** (Sermonti) and the **Object** (Theoretical Biology Forum) both appear in the evidence keys, the system infers that the relationship asserted in the claim (that he edited it) is **SUPPORTED**. The "Strict Matching" rule applies to **attributes** (like specific locations, dates, or counts) that differ from the evidence, but **does not** apply to the **existence of the relationship itself** if the entities are present.

**Refined Strategy:**
1.  **Entity Presence Check**: Are the Subject and Object entities present in the evidence keys?
2.  **Attribute/Constraint Check**: Does the claim assert a specific attribute (Location, Date, Count, Specific Role description) that **contradicts** or is **missing** from the evidence?
    *   If the claim says "Born in X" and evidence has "Born in Y" (or just "Y"), it is `NOT_SUPPORTED` (Mismatch).
    *   If the claim says "Wrote 4 books" and evidence only has names, it is `NOT_SUPPORTED` (Missing specific quantifier).
    *   If the claim says "Edited X" and evidence has "Sermonti" and "X", and no contradictory info exists, it is `SUPPORTED` (Co-occurrence implies the relationship).

Here is the new instruction incorporating this domain-specific logic.

```markdown
# Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence keys.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or specific fact) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context. It does **NOT** mean the information is missing or invalid.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Co-occurrence vs. Attribute" Rule
The task requires distinguishing between **Relationship Validation** and **Attribute Validation**.

#### A. Relationship Validation (Co-occurrence is Sufficient)
If a claim asserts a **defining relationship** or **role** between two entities (e.g., "X edited Y", "X broke Y's record", "X is the author of Y"), the claim is **SUPPORTED** if:
1.  The **Subject** entity (X) is present in the Evidence keys.
2.  The **Object** entity (Y) is present in the Evidence keys.
3.  **No contradictory evidence** exists (e.g., the evidence does not list a different editor or record holder).
*   *Logic*: In this specific dataset, the simultaneous presence of the two primary entities in the evidence keys implies the relationship asserted in the claim is true. You do **NOT** need a separate key explicitly stating "X edited Y".

#### B. Attribute Validation (Strict Matching Required)
If a claim asserts a **specific attribute**, **location**, **quantity**, or **date** that is distinct from the entity names themselves, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** unless the evidence explicitly contains that specific attribute.
*   **Location Mismatch**: If the claim says "Born in [Location A]" but the evidence key is "[Location B]" (even if Location B is in the same country), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    *   *Example*: Claim: "Born in New York County". Evidence: "Hoosick, New York". -> **NOT_SUPPORTED** (Specific location key missing).
*   **Quantity/Specific Detail Mismatch**: If the claim says "Wrote 4 books" or "Included in repertoire", and the evidence only lists the names of the people/composers, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    *   *Example*: Claim: "Ardoin wrote 4 books about Callas". Evidence: "John Ardoin", "Maria Callas". -> **NOT_SUPPORTED** (The specific count "4" is not in the evidence).
    *   *Example*: Claim: "Bellini in Callas's repertoire". Evidence: "Vincenzo Bellini", "Maria Callas". -> **NOT_SUPPORTED** (The specific relationship "repertoire" is not explicitly validated by names alone in this context, unlike the "Editor" or "Record Breaker" cases).

### 3. Decision Rule Summary
- **SUPPORTED**:
    - The claim asserts a relationship between X and Y, AND both X and Y are present in the evidence keys, AND no specific attribute (location/count) is asserted that contradicts the evidence.
    - The claim asserts a specific attribute (Location X, Count N), AND the evidence contains a key explicitly matching that attribute (e.g., "New York County" or "4 books").
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**:
    - The claim asserts a specific attribute (Location, Count, Date) that is **missing** from the evidence keys.
    - The claim asserts a specific attribute that **contradicts** the evidence keys (e.g., Claim says "Location A", Evidence has "Location B").
    - The claim asserts a relationship where the evidence keys are insufficient to imply the specific context (e.g., "repertoire" or "4 books" where only names are present).

## Reasoning Steps
1.  **Deconstruct the Claim**: Identify the **Subject**, **Object**, and the **Predicate**.
    *   Is the Predicate a **Relationship** (e.g., "edited", "broke record")?
    *   Is the Predicate an **Attribute** (e.g., "born in [Location]", "wrote [Number] books", "in [Context]")?
2.  **Scan Evidence**:
    *   Check for the presence of the Subject and Object keys.
    *   Check for the presence of the specific Attribute key (if applicable).
3.  **Apply Logic**:
    *   **If Relationship**: Are both entities present? If yes -> **SUPPORTED** (unless a specific contradictory attribute exists).
    *   **If Attribute**: Is the specific attribute key present? If no, or if a different attribute is present -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**: State the final verdict clearly.

## Example Application

### Case 1: Relationship Validation (SUPPORTED)
- **Claim**: "Giuseppe Sermonti was the Italian professor of genetics who edited the Theoretical Biological Forum."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Theoretical Biology Forum', 'value': 2}`, `{'key': 'Giuseppe Sermonti', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - **Predicate**: "edited" (Relationship).
    - **Entities**: "Giuseppe Sermonti" (Subject) and "Theoretical Biology Forum" (Object).
    - **Check**: Both entities are present in the evidence keys.
    - **Logic**: The claim asserts a defining role (editor). In this dataset, the co-occurrence of the person and the publication implies the relationship is true. No specific location or count is asserted that is missing.
    - **Verdict**: **SUPPORTED**

### Case 2: Location Mismatch (NOT_SUPPORTED)
- **Claim**: "Politician Lyman Sherwood was born in the New York county called New York."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Lyman Sherwood', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Hoosick, New York', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - **Predicate**: "born in" (Attribute: Location).
    - **Assertion**: "New York county called New York".
    - **Evidence**: Contains "Hoosick, New York".
    - **Logic**: The specific location key "New York county" is missing. "Hoosick" is a different entity. Co-occurrence of the person and a different location does not support the specific location claim.
    - **Verdict**: **NOT_SUPPORTED**

### Case 3: Quantity/Context Mismatch (NOT_SUPPORTED)
- **Claim**: "The Greek composer Vincenzo Bellini was included in the repertoire of the singer who had four books

Iteration 8 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence list.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- The integer `value` associated with a key is **irrelevant** to the verification logic.
- A `value` of `0`, `1`, `2`, or any integer simply indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **exists and is relevant** in the source context.
- **Do not** interpret `0` as "missing," "false," or "invalid." Treat any presence of a key as a positive confirmation of that entity's existence in the context.

### 2. The "Entity Resolution" Step (Crucial)
Before checking for presence, you must resolve the entities mentioned in the claim to the entities listed in the evidence keys:
- **Direct Match**: If the claim mentions a proper name (e.g., "Thutmose III") that appears exactly in the evidence keys, mark it as **Found**.
- **Descriptive Resolution**: If the claim uses a descriptive phrase (e.g., "the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty") or a specific identifier (e.g., "TT31"), you must determine if this description refers to an entity present in the evidence keys.
    - *Example*: If the claim mentions "Khonsu" but the evidence only lists "TT31", and "TT31" is the tomb/identifier for Khonsu, you must treat "Khonsu" as **Found** because the evidence contains the specific identifier for that entity.
    - *Example*: If the claim mentions "the sixth Pharaoh" and the evidence lists "Thutmose III", you must resolve "the sixth Pharaoh" to "Thutmose III" and mark it as **Found**.
- **Goal**: The goal is to verify if the *concept* or *entity* described in the claim is represented in the evidence, not just if the exact string matches.

### 3. Verification Strategy (The "Entity Presence" Rule)
Once entities are resolved:
1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the primary nouns/names that define the *subject* of the claim (e.g., specific people, titles of works, events, specific objects, or their unique identifiers).
2.  **Filter Attributes**: Ignore secondary attributes, modifiers, or relationship terms (such as specific publishers, producers, award names, dates, percentages, or causal links) **unless** the claim is exclusively about that attribute.
    - *Example*: In "Ballarat Bitter is a 4.9% beer...", "4.9%" is an attribute. "Ballarat Bitter" is the Core Subject.
3.  **Decision Rule**:
    - **SUPPORTED**: If **ALL** Core Subjects (after resolution) are found in the Evidence keys. The presence of the entities implies the validity of the claim's assertion in this dataset.
    - **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If **ANY** Core Subject (after resolution) is completely missing from the Evidence keys.

### 4. Reasoning Steps
1.  **Resolve Entities**: Map every entity mentioned in the claim to the corresponding `key` in the evidence. Use domain knowledge or contextual clues to link descriptive phrases or identifiers (like tomb numbers) to the entities they represent.
2.  **Scan Evidence**: Check if the resolved Core Subjects appear in the `key` field of the Evidence objects.
3.  **Apply Logic**:
    - If all Core Subjects are present (via direct match or resolution), conclude **SUPPORTED**.
    - If a Core Subject cannot be linked to any key in the evidence, conclude **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**: State the final verdict clearly as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic Application

### Case A: Descriptive Resolution (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Khonsu was the First Prophet to the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'TT31', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Thutmose III', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Khonsu" and "the sixth Pharaoh...".
    - Resolution: "the sixth Pharaoh..." resolves to "Thutmose III" (Found in evidence). "Khonsu" is not explicitly listed, but "TT31" (Theban Tomb 31) is the specific identifier for Khonsu's tomb. Therefore, the entity "Khonsu" is represented by "TT31".
    - Result: Both core concepts are present in the evidence.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Attribute Ignorance (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's Pulitzer Prize fiction novel."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Anthony Doerr" and "All the Light We Cannot See".
    - Attributes: "Scribner" (Publisher), "Pulitzer Prize" (Award).
    - Scan: Core subjects are present. Attributes are missing but ignored per the rules.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case C: Missing Core Subject (Not Supported)
- **Claim**: "The film 'Ocean's Eleven' was directed by Steven Soderbergh."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Ocean's Eleven', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Clooney', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Ocean's Eleven" and "Steven Soderbergh".
    - Scan: "Ocean's Eleven" is present. "Steven Soderbergh" is missing, and no identifier (like a production code) is present to resolve to him.
    - Result: A critical core subject is absent.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

Iteration 8 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence list.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **Existence Confirmation**: A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- **No Null Values**: A value of `0` does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat every entry in the evidence list as a confirmed presence of that entity.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Entity Presence & Identifier" Rule
The core logic of this task is that **the presence of the relevant entities in the evidence list implies the validity of the relationship described in the claim.** You do not need to verify the specific details (attributes, dates, or causal links) if the main entities are found.

#### Step A: Identify Core Subjects
Identify the primary nouns, names, or specific identifiers that define the *subject* of the claim.
- **Direct Names**: Explicit names (e.g., "Anthony Doerr", "McFarland, USA").
- **Descriptive Identifiers**: Descriptions that uniquely point to an entity (e.g., "the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty" refers to "Thutmose III").
- **Specific Codes/IDs**: Unique identifiers associated with an entity (e.g., "TT31" is the tomb code for "Khonsu"; "ISBN-123" for a book).
  - *Crucial*: If the claim mentions "Khonsu" and the evidence lists "TT31" (the tomb of Khonsu), this counts as the presence of "Khonsu". You must use external knowledge or logical inference to map the claim's entity to the evidence's identifier.

#### Step B: Scan Evidence for Matches
Check if the Core Subjects (or their unique identifiers/synonyms) appear in the `key` field of the Evidence.
- **Match Criteria**:
  1.  **Exact Match**: The key matches the claim text exactly.
  2.  **Identifier Match**: The key is a known unique identifier for the entity mentioned in the claim (e.g., Claim: "Khonsu", Evidence Key: "TT31").
  3.  **Descriptive Match**: The claim describes an entity that is named in the evidence (e.g., Claim: "the sixth Pharaoh...", Evidence Key: "Thutmose III").

#### Step C: Apply Decision Logic
- **SUPPORTED**: If **all** primary subject entities (or their unique identifiers/descriptions) are found in the Evidence keys.
  - *Note*: You do **NOT** need every single attribute, modifier, or relationship term (such as a specific publisher, producer, award name, or specific year) to appear as a separate key.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "Author X wrote Book Y published by Publisher Z", and the evidence contains "Author X" and "Book Y" but **not** "Publisher Z", the claim is **SUPPORTED**. The co-occurrence of the main entities implies the relationship is true in this context.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: Only if **one or more** of the **primary subject entities** (and their unique identifiers) are completely missing from the Evidence keys.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "Director X directed Movie Y", and the evidence contains "Movie Y" but **not** "Director X" (or any known identifier for Director X), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Reasoning Steps Template
1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the main entities. Explicitly note if any entity in the claim is represented in the evidence by a specific code, tomb number, or descriptive alias.
2.  **Scan Evidence**: Check for the presence of these subjects.
    - Did you find the name directly?
    - Did you find a unique identifier (e.g., a tomb code) that maps to the name?
    - Did you find a descriptive alias that maps to the name?
3.  **Evaluate Missing Attributes**: If any secondary details (publishers, specific dates, awards) are missing from the keys, explicitly state that this does **not** invalidate the claim per the Domain Logic.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**:
    - If all core subjects (via name, ID, or alias) are present: **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any core subject is entirely absent: **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic Application

### Case A: Identifier Mapping (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Khonsu was the First Prophet to the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'TT31', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Thutmose III', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Khonsu" and "Thutmose III" (identified by the description "sixth Pharaoh...").
    - Scan: "Thutmose III" is present. "Khonsu" is not present as a direct string, but "TT31" is present.
    - **Inference**: "TT31" is the specific tomb identifier for Khonsu. Therefore, the entity "Khonsu" is present in the evidence via its identifier.
    - Logic: Both core subjects are present (one by name, one by ID).
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Missing Attribute (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's Pulitzer Prize fiction novel."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Anthony Doerr" and "All the Light We Cannot See".
    - Attribute: "Scribner" (Publisher) is missing.
    - Logic: Core subjects are present. Missing publisher attribute does not trigger "NOT_SUPPORTED".
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case C: Missing Core Subject (Not Supported)
- **Claim**: "The film 'Ocean's Eleven' was directed by Steven Soderbergh."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Ocean's Eleven', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Clooney', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Ocean's Eleven" and "Steven Soderbergh".
    - Scan: "Ocean's Eleven" is present. "Steven Soderbergh" is missing, and no unique identifier (like a specific film code linked to him) is present.
    - Logic: A critical core subject is absent.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED
Iteration 8 [k=1]: Candidate score sum = 3.0 (best so far = 2.0)
Iteration 8 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or unique identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- It does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat `0` as a positive confirmation of existence.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Entity Presence & Identification" Rule
To verify a claim, you must determine if the **Core Subjects** of the claim are present in the Evidence.

**Step A: Identify Core Subjects**
- Extract the primary nouns, names, or entities that define the subject of the claim (e.g., specific people, titles of works, events, or specific objects).
- **Crucial Distinction**: Distinguish between the *entity itself* and its *attributes*.
  - *Entity*: "Khonsu", "Jefferson Davis", "Ballarat Bitter".
  - *Attribute*: "First Prophet", "Secretary of War", "4.9% ABV".
- Attributes do not need to appear as separate keys to support the claim.

**Step B: Scan Evidence with "Implicit Mapping"**
- Look for the Core Subjects in the `key` field of the Evidence.
- **Direct Match**: The exact name from the claim appears in the `key`.
- **Implicit Match (Domain Knowledge)**: If the exact name is missing, check if the `key` in the evidence is a **unique identifier** or **formal title** for the entity described in the claim.
  - *Example*: If the claim mentions "The tomb of Khonsu" but the evidence contains `TT31` (Theban Tomb 31), treat this as a **MATCH**. The evidence confirms the existence of the entity described.
  - *Example*: If the claim mentions "The film directed by Donovan Cook" and the evidence lists `Return to Never Land` (which is known to be directed by him in this context) or the director's name directly, treat as a **MATCH**.
- **Failure Condition**: The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** ONLY if the Core Subject (or its unique identifier) is completely absent from the evidence keys.

**Step C: Apply Decision Logic**
- **SUPPORTED**: If the Core Subjects (via direct match or implicit mapping) are found in the Evidence keys. The presence of these entities implies the validity of the claim's assertion in this dataset, even if specific modifiers (publishers, dates, percentages) are missing from the keys.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If the Core Subjects are completely missing from the Evidence keys.

## Reasoning Steps Template

1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the main entities. Note if any are described descriptively (e.g., "The tomb of X") rather than by name.
2.  **Scan Evidence & Map**:
    - Check for direct name matches.
    - **Check for Implicit Matches**: If a name is missing, does a key in the evidence represent a unique ID, tomb number, or formal title for that entity? If yes, mark as **Found**.
3.  **Apply Logic**:
    - If all Core Subjects are **Found** (directly or implicitly): Conclude **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any Core Subject is **Missing** (no direct name and no valid unique ID found): Conclude **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**: State the final verdict clearly as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic Application

### Case A: Implicit Mapping (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Khonsu was the First Prophet to the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'TT31', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Thutmose III', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Khonsu" and "Thutmose III".
    - Scan: "Thutmose III" is a direct match. "Khonsu" is not a direct key.
    - **Implicit Mapping**: The key `TT31` refers to "Theban Tomb 31". In this domain, TT31 is the specific tomb of Khonsu. Therefore, the presence of `TT31` confirms the presence of the entity "Khonsu".
    - Logic: Both core entities are present (one directly, one via ID).
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Missing Attribute (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's Pulitzer Prize fiction novel."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Anthony Doerr" and "All the Light We Cannot See".
    - Attribute: "Scribner" (Publisher).
    - Scan: Both core subjects are present. "Scribner" is missing.
    - Logic: Attributes are not required keys. Core entities are present.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case C: Missing Core Subject (Not Supported)
- **Claim**: "The film 'Ocean's Eleven' was directed by Steven Soderbergh."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Ocean's Eleven', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Clooney', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Ocean's Eleven" and "Steven Soderbergh".
    - Scan: "Ocean's Eleven" is present. "Steven Soderbergh" is missing.
    - **Implicit Check**: Is there a unique ID (like a director code) for Soderbergh in the evidence? No. Only "George Clooney" (an actor) is present.
    - Logic: A critical core subject (the director) is absent.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

Iteration 9 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Based on the analysis of the provided examples, feedback, and the original instructions, here is the refined and comprehensive instruction set.

The key insight from the feedback (specifically Example 2) is that while the original instructions allowed for "external knowledge" to map identifiers (e.g., mapping "TT31" to "Khonsu"), the task actually requires a stricter interpretation: **The claim must be verifiable solely by the presence of the entities explicitly named or logically unambiguous within the evidence list.**

In Example 2, the assistant incorrectly used external knowledge to infer that *Strymon bazochii* controls the genus *Silybum*. The evidence contained both names, but the claim made a specific causal assertion ("introduced... to control"). The feedback indicates that simply having the entities present is **not** enough if the specific relationship (control) or the specific target genus (implied by the description) is not explicitly linked in the evidence. The claim in Example 2 also contained a comparative clause ("has more species than this genus") and a second clause about medication extraction. The failure suggests that if the claim relies on a complex chain of external facts to link the entities, it should be **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if the names exist in the list.

The refined instruction below clarifies that **Entity Presence** is the *only* condition for support, and **External Knowledge** should only be used for trivial identifier mapping (like "TT31" -> "Khonsu" where the ID is a direct synonym), not for inferring complex causal relationships or biological control histories not explicitly stated in the evidence keys.

```markdown
# Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based **strictly** on the provided evidence list.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **Existence Confirmation**: A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- **No Null Values**: A value of `0` does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat every entry in the evidence list as a confirmed presence of that entity.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Entity Presence & Identifier" Rule
The core logic of this task is that **the presence of the relevant entities in the evidence list implies the validity of the relationship described in the claim ONLY if the relationship is direct or the entities are explicitly linked by the claim's own description.**

#### Step A: Identify Core Subjects
Identify the primary nouns, names, or specific identifiers that define the *subject* of the claim.
- **Direct Names**: Explicit names (e.g., "Anthony Doerr", "McFarland, USA").
- **Descriptive Identifiers**: Descriptions that uniquely point to an entity (e.g., "the sixth Pharaoh..." refers to "Thutmose III").
- **Specific Codes/IDs**: Unique identifiers associated with an entity (e.g., "TT31" is the tomb code for "Khonsu").
  - *Crucial Constraint*: You may use **minimal external knowledge** only to map a claim's entity to a known unique identifier in the evidence (e.g., Claim: "Khonsu", Evidence Key: "TT31").
  - **Prohibition**: You **MUST NOT** use external knowledge to infer complex causal relationships, historical events, or biological functions (e.g., "Species A controls Species B") unless the evidence explicitly lists both species in a context that implies that specific relationship. If the claim relies on a complex chain of facts not present in the evidence keys, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

#### Step B: Scan Evidence for Matches
Check if the Core Subjects (or their unique identifiers/synonyms) appear in the `key` field of the Evidence.
- **Match Criteria**:
  1.  **Exact Match**: The key matches the claim text exactly.
  2.  **Identifier Match**: The key is a known unique identifier for the entity mentioned in the claim (e.g., Claim: "Khonsu", Evidence Key: "TT31").
  3.  **Descriptive Match**: The claim describes an entity that is named in the evidence (e.g., Claim: "the sixth Pharaoh...", Evidence Key: "Thutmose III").

#### Step C: Apply Decision Logic
- **SUPPORTED**: If **all** primary subject entities (or their unique identifiers/descriptions) are found in the Evidence keys **AND** the claim does not rely on complex external causal logic that is not explicitly supported by the co-occurrence of these entities.
  - *Note*: You do **NOT** need every single attribute, modifier, or relationship term (such as a specific publisher, producer, award name, or specific year) to appear as a separate key.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "Author X wrote Book Y published by Publisher Z", and the evidence contains "Author X" and "Book Y" but **not** "Publisher Z", the claim is **SUPPORTED**. The co-occurrence of the main entities implies the relationship is true in this context.
  - *Warning*: If the claim asserts a specific action (e.g., "introduced to control") or a complex comparison (e.g., "has more species than") that requires external knowledge to validate the link between two present entities, and that link is not explicitly defined in the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If **one or more** of the **primary subject entities** (and their unique identifiers) are completely missing from the Evidence keys **OR** if the claim relies on a complex relationship/fact that cannot be verified solely by the presence of the entity names.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "Director X directed Movie Y", and the evidence contains "Movie Y" but **not** "Director X" (or any known identifier for Director X), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  - *Example (Complex Logic)*: If the claim is "Species A was introduced to control Species B", and the evidence contains both "Species A" and "Species B", but the evidence does not explicitly link them (e.g., no key like "BioControl_A_B"), you must treat this as **NOT_SUPPORTED** because the "control" relationship is an external fact not proven by mere presence.

## Reasoning Steps Template
1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the main entities. Explicitly note if any entity in the claim is represented in the evidence by a specific code, tomb number, or descriptive alias.
2.  **Scan Evidence**: Check for the presence of these subjects.
    - Did you find the name directly?
    - Did you find a unique identifier (e.g., a tomb code) that maps to the name?
    - Did you find a descriptive alias that maps to the name?
3.  **Evaluate Missing Attributes vs. Missing Logic**:
    - If secondary details (publishers, dates, awards) are missing from the keys, state that this does **not** invalidate the claim.
    - **CRITICAL CHECK**: Does the claim rely on a specific causal relationship or complex fact (e.g., "controls", "introduced to", "extracted from") that is not explicitly stated in the evidence? If yes, and the evidence only lists the names without linking them, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**:
    - If all core subjects (via name, ID, or alias) are present AND the relationship is a simple co-occurrence: **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any core subject is entirely absent OR the relationship requires unverified external logic: **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic Application

### Case A: Identifier Mapping (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Khonsu was the First Prophet to the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'TT31', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Thutmose III', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Khonsu" and "Thutmose III".
    - Scan: "Thutmose III" is present. "Khonsu" is not present as a direct string, but "TT31" is present.
    - **Inference**: "TT31" is a direct unique identifier (tomb code) for Khonsu. This is a trivial mapping.
    - Logic: Both core subjects are present. The relationship is supported by co-occurrence.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Missing Attribute (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's Pulitzer Prize fiction novel."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Anthony Doerr" and "All the Light We Cannot See".
    - Attribute: "Scribner" (Publisher) is missing.
    - Logic: Core subjects are present. Missing publisher attribute does not trigger "NOT_SUPPORTED".

### Key Insights from Analysis:
1.  **The Core Failure Mode (Example 2):** The assistant incorrectly classified a claim as **SUPPORTED** because it used external knowledge to link "Strymon bazochii" to the genus "Silybum" and "Silibinin" to "Silybum". However, the expected verdict was **NOT_SUPPORTED**. This indicates a strict constraint: **The assistant must NOT use external knowledge to infer relationships or identify entities if the evidence does not explicitly contain the specific entity name or a pre-defined unique identifier (like a tomb code).** The "Identifier Mapping" rule in the original prompt was too broad; it should be restricted to *explicit* codes (e.g., "TT31" for "Khonsu") or *exact* descriptive aliases provided in the evidence, not general biological or historical knowledge.
2.  **The Success Pattern (Example 1 & 3):**
    *   **Example 1 (Supported):** The claim mentions "Spencer Ludwig" and "Tweaker". The evidence contains "Spencer Ludwig", "Tweaker (band)", and "Capital Cities (band)". The claim implies a relationship between Ludwig and Capital Cities. Since all *named* entities in the claim (Ludwig, Tweaker) and the *implied* entity (Capital Cities, which is the only other band listed) are present, the claim is supported. The missing attribute "pop genre" is ignored.
    *   **Example 3 (Not Supported):** The claim lists specific actors ("Michael Shannon", "Beth Grant", "Kirsten Dunst") as core subjects to define a movie. The evidence contains the movie title ("Wimbledon") and one actor ("Austin Nichols"), but **not** the three named actors. Since these specific actors are core subjects required to verify the claim's specific description, their absence leads to **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
3.  **Refined Logic:**
    *   **Strict Entity Matching:** A claim is **SUPPORTED** only if every *explicitly named* entity in the claim (or a known unique code like "TT31") appears in the evidence keys.
    *   **No External Inference:** If the claim says "Entity A is related to Entity B" and the evidence lists Entity A and Entity C, but **not** Entity B, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if the assistant knows A and B are related in the real world. The evidence list is the *only* source of truth for entity presence.
    *   **Attribute vs. Entity:** Missing attributes (dates, genres, descriptions) do not cause a "Not Supported" verdict. Missing *Core Entities* (names of people, places, specific works) do.

Here is the new instruction:

```markdown
# Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based **strictly** on the provided evidence list.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **Existence Confirmation**: A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- **No Null Values**: A value of `0` does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat every entry in the evidence list as a confirmed presence of that entity.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Strict Entity Presence" Rule
The core logic of this task is that **the claim is only SUPPORTED if every specific entity explicitly named in the claim (or its unique identifier) is found in the Evidence keys.**

**Crucial Constraint**: You **MUST NOT** use external knowledge to infer relationships or identify entities.
- If the claim mentions "Entity A" and "Entity B", both must appear in the evidence keys (either as exact names or unique identifiers).
- If the claim implies a relationship (e.g., "Entity A is the genus of Entity B") but the evidence only lists "Entity A" and "Entity C" (where C is a different entity), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if you know from external knowledge that A and B are related.
- **Exception for Unique Identifiers**: You may map a claim entity to an evidence key **ONLY** if the evidence key is a well-known, unique code specifically associated with that entity (e.g., "TT31" for "Khonsu", "ISBN-123" for a specific book). You cannot map based on general descriptive knowledge (e.g., you cannot assume "Strymon bazochii" maps to "Silybum" just because you know they are biologically related; "Silybum" must be explicitly named in the claim or linked via a specific code).

#### Step A: Identify Core Subjects
Identify the primary nouns, names, or specific identifiers that define the *subject* of the claim.
- **Direct Names**: Explicit names (e.g., "Anthony Doerr", "McFarland, USA", "Michael Shannon").
- **Descriptive Identifiers**: Descriptions that uniquely point to an entity **only if** the evidence contains the specific name of that entity.
- **Specific Codes/IDs**: Unique identifiers associated with an entity (e.g., "TT31" for "Khonsu").
  - *Warning*: Do not use general knowledge to bridge gaps. If the claim says "The genus of X" and the evidence lists "Y", but the claim does not name "Y" explicitly, you cannot assume "Y" is the genus unless "Y" is the only logical option and the claim implies "Y" is the subject. However, if the claim names specific actors or specific entities, those names must be in the evidence.

#### Step B: Scan Evidence for Matches
Check if the Core Subjects appear in the `key` field of the Evidence.
- **Match Criteria**:
  1.  **Exact Match**: The key matches the claim text exactly (or with minor normalization like removing "(band)").
  2.  **Identifier Match**: The key is a known unique identifier for the entity mentioned in the claim (e.g., Claim: "Khonsu", Evidence Key: "TT31").
  3.  **No Inference**: If the claim mentions "Entity X" and the evidence does not contain "Entity X" (or its unique ID), the entity is considered **MISSING**. Do not assume the entity is present because it is related to another entity in the evidence.

#### Step C: Apply Decision Logic
- **SUPPORTED**: If **all** primary subject entities explicitly named in the claim (or their unique identifiers) are found in the Evidence keys.
  - *Note*: You do **NOT** need every single attribute, modifier, or relationship term (such as a specific publisher, producer, award name, specific year, or genre) to appear as a separate key.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "Author X wrote Book Y published by Publisher Z", and the evidence contains "Author X" and "Book Y" but **not** "Publisher Z", the claim is **SUPPORTED**. The co-occurrence of the main entities implies the relationship is true in this context.

- **NOT_SUPPORTED**: If **one or more** of the **primary subject entities** (names of people, specific works, specific places) are completely missing from the Evidence keys.
  - *Example*: If the claim is "The movie with actors A, B, and C is a comedy", and the evidence contains "Movie X" and "Actor A" but **not** "Actor B" or "Actor C", the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**. The missing actors are core subjects required to verify the specific description.
  - *Example (External Knowledge Trap)*: If the claim is "Entity A is related to Entity B", and the evidence contains "Entity A" and "Entity C" (but not B), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if you know A and B are related in the real world.

## Reasoning Steps Template
1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the main entities **explicitly named** in the claim.
    - *Critical Check*: Are there any entities mentioned in the claim that are NOT in the evidence?
    - *Critical Check*: Are you trying to use external knowledge to link two entities that are not both explicitly present? If so, stop.
2.  **Scan Evidence**: Check for the presence of these subjects.
    - Did you find the name directly?
    - Did you find a unique identifier (e.g., a tomb code) that maps to the name?
    - **Do NOT** assume an entity is present based on a relationship with another entity in the evidence.
3.  **Evaluate Missing Attributes**: If any secondary details (publishers, specific dates, genres, awards) are missing from the keys, explicitly state that this does **not** invalidate the claim per the Domain Logic.
4.  **Formulate Conclusion**:
    - If all core subjects (via name, ID, or explicit alias) are present: **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any core subject is entirely absent (and not covered by a unique ID): **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic

Iteration 9 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Based on the analysis of the provided examples and feedback, here is the refined instruction for the assistant.

The key insight derived from the examples (specifically Example 2) is that while the "Entity Presence" rule is powerful, it **cannot** be used to validate claims that rely on **complex comparative logic** (e.g., "Genus A has more species than Genus B") or **specific factual assertions about attributes** (e.g., "introduced in 1902", "discovered in 1925") if those specific facts are not explicitly represented in the evidence keys.

In Example 2, the assistant incorrectly marked the claim as `SUPPORTED` simply because the entities (Strymon, Silybum, Silibinin) were present. However, the claim makes specific factual assertions about **comparative species counts** and **historical dates** that are not present in the evidence. The "Missing Attribute" rule (which says missing publishers don't matter) applies to **secondary modifiers** of a confirmed relationship, not to the **core factual predicates** of the claim itself. If the claim is *about* the comparison or the date, and the evidence lacks the keys to verify that specific fact, the claim is `NOT_SUPPORTED`.

Here is the updated instruction:

```markdown
# Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence list.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name, concept, or identifier) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- **Existence Confirmation**: A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- **No Null Values**: A value of `0` does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat every entry in the evidence list as a confirmed presence of that entity.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Entity Presence & Identifier" Rule
The core logic of this task is that **the presence of the relevant entities in the evidence list implies the validity of the relationship described in the claim**, *provided the claim is a simple assertion of existence or association.*

#### Step A: Identify Core Subjects
Identify the primary nouns, names, or specific identifiers that define the *subject* of the claim.
- **Direct Names**: Explicit names (e.g., "Anthony Doerr", "McFarland, USA").
- **Descriptive Identifiers**: Descriptions that uniquely point to an entity (e.g., "the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty" refers to "Thutmose III").
- **Specific Codes/IDs**: Unique identifiers associated with an entity (e.g., "TT31" is the tomb code for "Khonsu"; "ISBN-123" for a book).
  - *Crucial*: If the claim mentions "Khonsu" and the evidence lists "TT31" (the tomb of Khonsu), this counts as the presence of "Khonsu". You must use external knowledge or logical inference to map the claim's entity to the evidence's identifier.

#### Step B: Scan Evidence for Matches
Check if the Core Subjects (or their unique identifiers/synonyms) appear in the `key` field of the Evidence.
- **Match Criteria**:
  1.  **Exact Match**: The key matches the claim text exactly.
  2.  **Identifier Match**: The key is a known unique identifier for the entity mentioned in the claim.
  3.  **Descriptive Match**: The claim describes an entity that is named in the evidence.

#### Step C: Apply Decision Logic (Crucial Distinction)

**Scenario 1: Simple Association (SUPPORTED)**
- **Condition**: The claim asserts that Entity A is related to Entity B (e.g., "A wrote B", "A is a member of B", "A was published by C").
- **Rule**: If **all** primary subject entities (A and B) are found in the Evidence keys, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Exception for Attributes**: You do **NOT** need every single attribute, modifier, or relationship term (such as a specific publisher, producer, award name, or specific year) to appear as a separate key.
  - *Example*: Claim: "Author X wrote Book Y published by Publisher Z". Evidence: ["Author X", "Book Y"]. Verdict: **SUPPORTED**. (The missing "Publisher Z" is a secondary attribute; the core relationship "Author X wrote Book Y" is supported by the presence of the two main entities).

**Scenario 2: Complex Predicates or Comparisons (NOT_SUPPORTED)**
- **Condition**: The claim makes a specific factual assertion that **cannot** be inferred solely from the co-occurrence of entities. This includes:
  - **Comparative Statements**: Claims comparing quantities, sizes, or counts (e.g., "Genus A has **more species** than Genus B").
  - **Specific Historical Facts**: Claims relying on specific dates, years, or locations that are the *main point* of the claim (e.g., "introduced in **1902**", "discovered in **1925**").
  - **Negative Constraints**: Claims asserting what an entity is *not* (e.g., "Tweaker is **not** in the pop genre").
- **Rule**: If the claim relies on these specific predicates, and the evidence list **does not contain keys** representing those specific facts (e.g., a key for "1902", a key for "species count", or a key for "pop genre"), the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
  - *Reasoning*: The mere presence of "Genus A" and "Genus B" in the evidence proves they exist, but it does **not** prove the specific relationship (comparison of species count) or the specific date. The evidence is insufficient to verify the *predicate* of the claim.
  - *Example*: Claim: "Genus A has more species than Genus B." Evidence: ["Genus A", "Genus B"]. Verdict: **NOT_SUPPORTED**. (The evidence confirms the entities exist, but provides no data to verify the comparison).

## Reasoning Steps Template
1.  **Identify Core Subjects**: List the main entities. Explicitly note if any entity in the claim is represented in the evidence by a specific code, tomb number, or descriptive alias.
2.  **Analyze Claim Type**: Determine if the claim is a **Simple Association** (Scenario 1) or a **Complex Predicate** (Scenario 2).
    - *Check*: Does the claim rely on a specific comparison, date, or negative attribute as its primary truth condition?
3.  **Scan Evidence**: Check for the presence of these subjects.
    - Did you find the name directly?
    - Did you find a unique identifier (e.g., a tomb code) that maps to the name?
4.  **Evaluate Missing Attributes**:
    - **If Simple Association**: Missing secondary details (publishers, specific years in a "published by" context) do **not** invalidate the claim.
    - **If Complex Predicate**: Missing keys for the specific comparison, date, or negative attribute **DO** invalidate the claim.
5.  **Formulate Conclusion**:
    - If all core subjects are present AND the claim type allows for inference (Simple Association): **SUPPORTED**.
    - If any core subject is entirely absent OR the claim relies on a specific fact/predicate not present in the evidence keys: **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Examples of Logic Application

### Case A: Identifier Mapping (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Khonsu was the First Prophet to the sixth Pharaoh of the Eighteenth Dynasty."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'TT31', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'Thutmose III', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Khonsu" (mapped to TT31) and "Thutmose III".
    - Scan: Both entities are present (one by name, one by ID).
    - Claim Type: Simple Association (Role assignment).
    - Logic: Co-occurrence of the entities supports the relationship.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Missing Attribute (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's Pulitzer Prize fiction novel."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    - Core Subjects: "Anthony Doerr" and "All the Light We Cannot See".
    - Attribute: "Scribner" is missing.
    - Claim Type: Simple Association (Publication).
    - Logic: Core subjects are present. Missing publisher attribute does not trigger "NOT_SUPPORTED" because the core relationship (Author -> Book) is established by the entities.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case C: Missing Core Subject (Not Supported)
- **Claim**: "The film 'Ocean's Eleven' was directed by Steven Soderbergh."

### Key Insights & Logic Extraction
1.  **The "Entity Presence" Heuristic**: The core logic is not about verifying the *truth* of the claim against external knowledge, but verifying if the *entities mentioned in the claim exist in the provided evidence list*.
2.  **Distinction Between "Core Subjects" and "Attributes"**:
    *   **Core Subjects**: The primary nouns/names that define the existence of the entities (e.g., "George Whitefield", "Charles Wesley", "Doc Hollywood", "Michael Caton-Jones"). If these are missing, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    *   **Attributes/Modifiers**: Descriptive terms, roles, or secondary entities that provide context (e.g., "plants", "Pulitzer Prize", "Scribner", "associate producer"). If these are missing, the claim is **SUPPORTED** (provided the Core Subjects are present).
3.  **The "John Wesley" vs. "Charles Wesley" Trap (Example 1)**:
    *   In Example 1, the claim mentions "Charles Wesley". The evidence contains "John Wesley". The assistant initially failed because it might have assumed "Wesley" was close enough or that the presence of "Methodism" and "Edward Perronet" was sufficient.
    *   **Correction**: The feedback indicates that **exact string matching** for specific named entities is required. "John Wesley" does **not** satisfy the requirement for "Charles Wesley". They are distinct core subjects. The claim requires *both* George Whitefield and Charles Wesley. Since both are missing (only John is present), the claim should technically be `NOT_SUPPORTED` based on strict logic, **BUT** the feedback says the expected verdict is `SUPPORTED`.
    *   **Re-evaluation of Example 1**: Why is Example 1 `SUPPORTED`?
        *   Claim: "George Whitefield, Charles Wesley and the priest who worked with Edward Perronet started..."
        *   Evidence: `Methodism`, `John Wesley`, `Edward Perronet`, `St Peter's, Eastern Hill`.
        *   Wait, the feedback says "Incorrect. Extracted verdict 'not_supported' does not match expected 'supported'."
        *   This implies the logic is **NOT** "All named entities must be present."
        *   **Revised Logic for Example 1**: The claim is a complex narrative. The "Core Subject" of the *entire* claim might be the "Methodist movement" or the "priest who worked with Edward Perronet".
        *   *Hypothesis*: The task is to verify if the **main topic** or the **central relationship** is supported. If the claim lists a group of people, and the evidence contains *some* of them plus the central concept (Methodism), does it count?
        *   *Alternative Hypothesis (The "Subject of the Sentence" Rule)*: In Example 1, the sentence structure is "George Whitefield, Charles Wesley and [the priest...] started...". The subject is a compound list.

### Analysis of Task Requirements & Edge Cases
1.  **Core Logic**: The task is an **Entity Presence Verification**. The goal is not to fact-check the *truth* of the claim against external knowledge, but to determine if the *entities* mentioned in the claim exist within the provided evidence list.
2.  **The "Zero" Value Trap**: A `value` of `0` (or any integer) in the evidence indicates **presence**, not absence. This is a critical domain rule that must be explicitly stated to prevent the model from treating `0` as "no data."
3.  **The "Missing Attribute" vs. "Missing Core Subject" Distinction**:
    *   **Attributes (Ignore for Missing Checks)**: Modifiers, roles, publishers, producers, or specific relationship descriptors (e.g., "Scribner", "Pulitzer Prize", "Producer") do **not** need to appear as keys. If the main entities (Author, Book) are present, the claim is **SUPPORTED**, even if the publisher is missing from the keys.
    *   **Core Subjects (Strict Check)**: The primary nouns defining the *who* or *what* of the claim (e.g., specific people like "George Whitefield", specific works like "Doc Hollywood", specific organizations) **MUST** appear in the evidence keys.

Iteration 10 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Claim Verification based on Entity Evidence

## Objective
Determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based strictly on the provided evidence.

## Input Format
- **Evidence**: A list of JSON-like objects containing `key` (an entity name or concept) and `value` (an integer score).
- **Claim**: A natural language sentence making a factual assertion.

## Critical Domain Logic (Read Carefully)

### 1. Interpretation of Evidence Values
- A `value` of `0` (or any integer) indicates that the entity listed in the `key` **is present and relevant** to the source context.
- It does **NOT** mean the information is missing, absent, or invalid. Treat `0` as a positive confirmation of existence.

### 2. Verification Strategy: The "Topic & Co-occurrence" Rule
To determine the verdict, you must distinguish between **General Topic Claims** and **Specific Instance Claims**.

#### A. For General Topic Claims (Historical Origins, Movements, Categories)
*Example: "X, Y, and Z started the [Movement]..." or "A and B are [Category]..."*
- **Core Logic**: If the **Main Topic** (e.g., "Methodism", "Plants") is present in the evidence, AND **at least one other relevant entity** mentioned in the claim OR a **closely related entity** (e.g., a primary figure associated with the topic) is present, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Name Substitution Tolerance**: You do **NOT** require every specific name listed in the claim to appear as a key.
    - *Scenario*: If the claim says "George Whitefield and Charles Wesley started Methodism," but the evidence only contains "John Wesley" and "Methodism," the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
    - *Reasoning*: The presence of the topic ("Methodism") and a key figure associated with it ("John Wesley") confirms the context of the claim. The absence of the other names does not invalidate the general assertion about the movement's origin in the source context.
- **Decision**: If the Main Topic is present + (Any named entity from claim OR a highly related entity from the domain) is present -> **SUPPORTED**.

#### B. For Specific Instance Claims (Specific Works, Events, Relationships)
*Example: "The film 'X' was directed by Y..." or "Z was the producer of W..."*
- **Core Logic**: These claims rely on specific, unique identifiers to define the instance.
- **Mandatory Entities**: The **Primary Subject** (e.g., the specific film title) AND the **Specific Attribute Subject** (e.g., the specific director, producer, or author named in the claim) must both be present in the evidence keys.
- **Missing Entity Rule**: If the specific person/entity performing the action (e.g., "Michael Caton-Jones" as the director) is **missing** from the evidence keys, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**, even if the work title is present.
- **Reasoning**: In these cases, the specific name is not just an attribute; it is the defining characteristic of the specific instance being verified. Its absence means the evidence cannot confirm the specific relationship asserted.

### 3. Reasoning Steps
1.  **Classify the Claim**: Determine if the claim is a **General Topic Claim** (broad movement/category) or a **Specific Instance Claim** (specific work/event with a unique agent).
2.  **Identify Entities**:
    -   Extract the **Main Topic** (if General) or **Primary Subject** (if Specific).
    -   Extract the **Named Agents** (people, specific roles) mentioned in the claim.
3.  **Scan Evidence**:
    -   Check if the Main Topic/Primary Subject is in the `key` list.
    -   Check if the Named Agents are in the `key` list.
    -   *Crucial Check for General Claims*: If specific agents are missing, check for **Related Entities** (e.g., if "George Whitefield" is missing, is "John Wesley" present?).
4.  **Apply Logic**:
    -   **General Topic Claim**:
        -   If Main Topic is present AND (Named Agent present OR Related Entity present) -> **SUPPORTED**.
        -   If Main Topic is missing -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
    -   **Specific Instance Claim**:
        -   If Primary Subject is present AND **ALL** specific Named Agents (directors, specific producers, etc.) are present -> **SUPPORTED**.
        -   If Primary Subject is present BUT **ANY** specific Named Agent is missing -> **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
5.  **Formulate Conclusion**: State the final verdict clearly as either **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

## Example Application

### Case A: General Topic Claim (Supported despite missing names)
- **Claim**: "George Whitefield, Charles Wesley and the priest who worked with Edward Perronet started the Methodist movement."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Methodism', 'value': 2}`, `{'key': 'John Wesley', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Edward Perronet', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    -   **Classification**: General Topic Claim (origin of a movement).
    -   **Scan**: "Methodism" (Main Topic) is present. "Edward Perronet" (Named Agent) is present. "John Wesley" (Related Entity) is present. "George Whitefield" and "Charles Wesley" are missing.
    -   **Logic**: Since the Main Topic ("Methodism") is present and a Related Entity ("John Wesley") who is historically central to the movement is also present, the context supports the claim. The absence of the other names does not negate the general assertion.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Case B: Specific Instance Claim (Not Supported due to missing specific agent)
- **Claim**: "The film 'Doc Hollywood' was directed by Michael Caton-Jones."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Doc Hollywood', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'George Hamilton', 'value': 1}`
- **Reasoning**:
    -   **Classification**: Specific Instance Claim (specific film + specific director).
    -   **Scan**: "Doc Hollywood" (Primary Subject) is present. "Michael Caton-Jones" (Specific Agent) is **Missing**.
    -   **Logic**: For specific works, the director is a defining unique identifier. The absence of the specific director's name in the evidence means the specific relationship cannot be verified.
- **Verdict**: NOT_SUPPORTED

### Case C: Specific Instance Claim (Supported)
- **Claim**: "Scribner published Anthony Doerr's novel 'All the Light We Cannot See'."
- **Evidence**: `{'key': 'Anthony Doerr', 'value': 1}`, `{'key': 'All the Light We Cannot See', 'value': 0}`, `{'key': 'Scribner', 'value': 0}`
- **Reasoning**:
    -   **Classification**: Specific Instance Claim (Author + Book + Publisher).
    -   **Scan**: All three specific entities (Author, Book, Publisher) are present.
    -   **Logic**: All required specific entities are found.
- **Verdict**: SUPPORTED

### Analysis of Task Logic & Errors
1.  **The Core Mechanism**: The task is a **binary entity existence check**. The claim is **SUPPORTED** if and only if **every** specific noun phrase, entity name, or proper noun mentioned in the claim exists as a `key` in the provided Evidence list.
2.  **The "Value" Trap**: The integer `value` (0 or 1) is **irrelevant** to the truth of the claim. It simply indicates the entity is present in the source context. The assistant must ignore the semantic meaning of "0" (often interpreted as "false" or "zero") and treat it as "Present".
3.  **The "Missing Entity" Rule (Example 2)**: In Example 2, the claim mentioned "Evergreen". The evidence contained "Advanced Micro Devices", "Level 3 Communications", and "Radeon HD 5000 Series", but **not** "Evergreen". The assistant correctly identified "Evergreen" was missing but concluded `NOT_SUPPORTED`. However, the feedback said the expected answer was `SUPPORTED`.
    *   *Correction/Inference*: This implies that **general descriptors or specific modifiers** (like "Evergreen" as a GPU codename) might be considered **non-critical** if the **primary subject entities** (Company, Product Series) are present. OR, more likely, the task logic is: **If the *main* entities are present, the claim is SUPPORTED, even if minor modifiers are missing.**

        *   The claim says: "The company produced the Evergreen GPU's for its Radeon HD 5000 Series."
        *   Evidence keys: `Advanced Micro Devices`, `Level 3 Communications`, `Radeon HD 5000 Series`.
        *   The entity "Evergreen" is missing.

It likely requires the **Subject** and the **Object/Context** to be present, but allows for **implicit attributes** (like "Evergreen" being a known attribute of the "Radeon HD 5000 Series" or "Advanced Micro Devices") to be inferred if the main entities are linked.
        *   *Contrast with Example 1*: In Example 1, the claim adds specific *new* facts (Emmy/Tony awards, specific role "fairy", specific episode number/season) that are **not** inherent to the entity "Swoosie Kurtz" or the episode title "Chuck Versus the Role Models" in a general knowledge sense, nor are they present in the keys.
        *   *Revised Logic*: The instruction "If all critical entities... are found" was too strict in Example 1 (leading to false support) and too loose in Example 2 (leading to false rejection).
        *   *The Real Pattern*: The task is likely **Entity Co-occurrence Verification**.
            *   If the claim asserts a **relationship** or **attribute** that is **not** explicitly represented by the presence of the entities in the evidence list, it is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
            *   Wait, Example 2 is the outlier. "Evergreen" is missing, yet it is SUPPORTED.
            *   Let's look at the claim structure again.
                *   Ex 1 Claim: "Swoosie Kurtz... was on [Episode] as a fairy." -> The "fairy" role is a specific attribute not in keys. Result: NOT_SUPPORTED.

            *   In Ex 2, the assistant thought "Evergreen" was a critical entity that was missing. The feedback says NO. "Evergreen" is **not** a critical entity that needs to be explicitly listed in the keys for the claim to be supported.
            *   *Conclusion*: The task requires the assistant to distinguish between **Core Entities** (Proper Nouns, specific subjects/objects that must be in the evidence) and **Descriptive Attributes** (Adjectives, roles, specific numbers, or synonyms that do not need to be in the evidence keys).
            *   *Refined Rule*: A claim is **SUPPORTED** if **all Proper Noun Entities** (Names of people, specific works, organizations, specific species) mentioned in the claim are present in the Evidence keys. **Descriptive details** (roles like "fairy", awards, specific numbers like "15", or technical codenames like "Evergreen" if the main product is listed) do **not** need to be present as keys.

            *   *Hypothesis*: The task is about **Entity Linking**.
                *   If the claim asserts a **relationship** (A did B), and the evidence only lists A and B, is it supported?
                *   Ex 1: A (Swoosie) was in B (Episode) as C (Fairy). Evidence has A and B. Missing C. -> NOT_SUPPORTED.

            *   Or, perhaps the claim in Ex 2 is "The company produced the Evergreen GPU's..." -> The entity "Evergreen" is the **object** of the production. The entity "Radeon HD 5000 Series" is the **series**.
            *   Maybe the rule is: **If the claim mentions a specific entity that is a subset or alias of an entity present in the evidence, it is SUPPORTED.**
                *   "Evergreen" is the codename for "Radeon HD 5000 Series". Since "Radeon HD 5000 Series" is in the evidence, the claim is supported.
                *   "Fairy" is NOT a subset or alias of "Chuck Versus the Role Models". It's a role played *in* the episode.
            *   This seems to be the key.
